< Review>
Food was excellent though portions were a little bit on the small side. Decor is beautiful with amazing elephant art!! The only reason they don't get five stars is one of their booths had a staple sticking out that cut one of the members of my party. We pointed out out to them and their response was not what I was expecting; we were really worried that someone else might get cut and they kind of ignored it. Though that might have been a language barrier, I'm not really sure. In their defense, they did bring over a first aid kit which was fairly well stocked.

The pad Thai was a little weird but yummy.  And the spice levels were a little on the low side, so definitely take that into account.</Review>

<user>112427237682604984265<//user><name>Stephen Cheevers</name><Time>1548785279171</Time><rating>5< /rating>< Text>
Visited recently on a work trip with some colleagues, dropping by just as it was getting dark. We took a table outside in the alley (much nicer than it sounds) and started off with drinks. The drinks were good, price was reasonable. Food is standard Irish pub food, good quality. Our waitress helped me acquire some curried chips which was a nice touch.

Overall, it's a good bar/restaurant, serving good quality food and they don't cheat on the drinks either, or water them down as far as we could tell. And we conducted a thorough test. Definitely recommended for an evening, or to drop in after work.

Pro tip: The bouncer/assistant/maitre'd who greets you when you walk up and helps you get a seat, looks EXACTLY like a customer so we didn't recognize at first that he worked there and tried to walk past him. But he was a good guy and fine about it.<//Text>

<Name>Justin Ryan< /Name><date>1533931679262<//date>< Rate>
1<//Rate>
< Text>
A wonderful place if you want to get physically assaulted by staff.

Went here for dinner. Got a hamburger and two beers. Prices were a bit high, service a bit tame, but nothing terrible.

Came back later for late night drinks around 10 pm or so. Bought a $7 beer with a 10 dollar bill. Immediately after I purchased, went to put in a couple of bucks in the jukebox machine to hear some good tunes. When I came back, change from my beer was missing despite my being gone for less than a minute. Every bar I've been to, from SF to LA to Europe to Asia, has my change waiting for me after I order a drink.

Not the Irish Bank, apparently.

I called out the bartender on it. He told me I disappeared, despite me going to the jukebox literally right around the corner in plain eyesight. We get into a back and forth, he becoming faux defensive about me using the F-word. He gets my change from the tip jar for some reason instead of the cash register, further implying he never thought I was coming back and wanted to pocket the money. We get into a verbal altercation, I throw a beer in his face, and I get kicked out.

I know, immature move on my part. But i thought that was the end of it. I was wrong.

I sit outside a block up from the bar, smoking a cigarette about 15 minutes after the encounter. Bartender from earlier walks up and asks me if I'm the same guy, I say yeah. He starts throwing wild punches at me and kicks me repeatedly. I try to defend myself but he's vicious, throwing everything he's got at me. Bystanders witness the whole thing and cops get called, bartender runs off into the night. I spend 30 minutes filing a police report, officers constantly asking if I want to go to a hospital or emergency room to take care of my black eye and busted lip. I say no, I can take care of it on my own. They ask me if I intend on pressing charges, I say yes.

There's a lot of bars in San Francisco, and a lot in this nearby area. Don't waste your time on the Irish Bank. You'll either get overcharged for a beer or will get physically assaulted from staff. Unless your Muhammad Ali or Ronda Rousey, it isn't worth it to come here to deal with the fights. Attached is a photo of my black eye, courtesy of The Irish Bank.</Text>

<response>None<//response><Text>This place is MUCH different than described in the online reviews.  I hoped it would become my new Irish social spot. (If you were a patron of Joxer Dalys at West Portal and Durty Nellies on Irvine St., you will recall the friendly greeting received upon entering the bars and your favorite beer immediately brought to you by chatty, personable staff who always acted happy to see you.) What I found was a small, somewhat dark, antiquated, interior with a bar wrapped around a wall, some old tables and chairs in the middle of the floor, and a few large beer barrels in the corner surrounded by stools sitting against the wall.  I was not greeted by the bar staff when I entered, although there were very few patrons inside, so I sat down at a table and waited for a sever to take my order.  Suddenly, a woman rushed past me without a glance or acknowledgment; upon returning she caught my eye and quickly blurted out that I had to order at  the bar.  So, I  got up and stood in front of the bar, and without any formal greeting, one said,  "what do you want to order?"  The so-called authentic, delicious, Irish breakfast  came about 20 minutes later, tossed onto my table by the same barman, who then quickly rushed back to the bar.  As I looked down, I was shocked by the sight that greeted my eyes: Two overcooked, brownish eggs, with greasy egg whites; a burnt, tiny, shriveled piece of bacon; 2 tiny pieces of hard, overcooked white/black pudding (I couldn't tell you which was which); a small serving of (canned) baked beans and a piece of toast.  I ate it because I was starving and because my intuition told me to not waste my energy complaining about the complete lack of food quality and culinary skills in the kitchen.  I didn't want the experience to be a total loss so I decided to sit at the bar and order a beer.  One of the barman looked at me and said,  "Ready to Rock and Roll?" and then plopped my tab in front of my face. When I told him that I actually wanted to order a beer, he made a small effort to stop me but my facial expression said it all, and he left it alone, without so much as a "see you again," or "thank you for coming," as I left.  What a waste of $15.00.  Never again.  Google also recommended Chieftains Irish Bar, located on Fifth Street, for great Irish breakfast, lunch, and drinks.  I'll try them tomorrow.  Maybe they'll serve me a beer.< /Text>< user_name>

I am Irish and when I tried to go in I was refused entry because I didn't have a "valid ID". <Rating>5<//Rating>< Text>
Hidden in an alleyway near Union Square with outdoor cafe seating in the street, you'll feel like you've left the US as you settle down with mates over a pint. The native favorites are all in abundance - from Shepherd's Pie and fish n' chips to Magner's, Smithwick's and Guiness tap. Table service is slow to a miss, but it is a fantastic pub with better-than-average food. Great for happy hour, groups, or just brooding over a beer at the bar. P.S. Keep an eye out for the confessional.</Text>

4< /rate>
<Text>Irish restaurants seem to be highly criticized everywhere i go, making me think they are either sub-par on the west coast as a whole and i havent been exposed to anything else... or people are just stupid and snobby for no reason. as far as i can tell, this food is simple, filling, cheap, pub-style food to absorb all the alcohol you are consuming. and for me, that is just fine.

we were strolling around the area deciding on dinner, and the lovely alleyway patio caught my eye. the tables are simple no frills patio tables and the lighting is red at night...making food photography terrible btw :/

i will keep this simple like the food and experience was:

app: blue cheese fries. yum. IF you like blue cheese which is plentiful

irish beef stew: for a warm night it normally wouldnt have been my choice, but i wanted something authentic and several people spoke highly of it so i gave it a go. i liked it a lot...even with a small appetite. i would have liked it a bit chunkier with the veggies but the flavor was good.

black n tan: i just have to get it anytime im at an irish pub. well made :)

dining partner got the reuben and it looked quite tasty.

service was good...food came out quick...busser was VERY enthusiastic and diligent, it was sweet. no complains<//Text>< pictures>
